               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202407274-sec-0050-title">2.3 Sodium Storage Mechanism</h3>
            
            <p>To further investigate the kinetic behavior of the NOCNTF-15 electrode in the sodium storage process, CV curves were recorded at different scan rates ranging from 0.1 to 3.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27a</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28a</a>, Supporting Information). According to previous research, the relationship between the peak current (<i>i</i>) and scan rate <i>(v)</i> in the CV curve can be described using equation: <i>i&nbsp;=&nbsp;a*v<sup>b</sup></i>, the <i>b</i> value is determined by plotting <i>log(v)</i> against <i>log(i)</i>, and this value provides an insight into the predominant charge storage mechanism during the charge and discharge processes. When the value of <i>b</i> is close to 0.5, the charge/discharge process is determined by the diffusion mechanism. When this value is close to 1, the charge/discharge process is determined by pseudocapacitive control.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407274-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407274-bib-0047_R_d91885445e1289" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - eScience">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to the calculation results, the <i>b</i> values of the cathode and anode peaks in the sodium-ion half cell assembled by Co@NCNTF-15 electrode were 0.85 and 0.8, respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27b</a>, Supporting Information), while those of the cathode and anode peaks by NOCNTF-15 electrode were 0.91 and 0.81, respectively (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28b</a>, Supporting Information). This implied that the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism in the NOCNTF-15 electrode was primarily governed by a pseudocapacitive controlled process, which was crucial for achieving excellent rate performance, especially under high current density conditions. In addition, the ratio of the pseudocapacitive contribution, as suggested by Dunn and Chao, can be calculated using the following equation: <i>i(v)&nbsp;=&nbsp;k<sub>1</sub> v&nbsp;+&nbsp;k<sub>2</sub> v<sup>1/2</sup></i>, Here, <i>k<sub>1</sub>v</i> and <i>k<sub>2</sub>v<sup>1/2</sup></i> represent the pseudocapacitive and diffusional contributions, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407274-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407274-bib-0048_R_d91885445e1324" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Adv. Energy Mater.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The pseudocapacitive contribution of Co@NCNTF-15 and NOCNTF-15 electrodes at a scan rate of 2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> are 82.72% and 84.61%, respectively (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27c</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28c</a>, Supporting Information). When the scan rate was increased from 0.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> to 3&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, the pseudocapacitive control contribution of the Co@NCNTF-15 electrode increased from 64.93% to 86.55% (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27d</a>, Supporting Information), while that of the NOCNTF-15 electrode increased from 66.77% to 91.45% (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28d</a>, Supporting Information). Obviously, compared to the Co@NCNTF-15 electrode, the NOCNTF-15 electrode had a higher pseudocapacitive control contribution during sodium storage, which was probably due to the many oxygen-containing groups of the CNTs, leading to a rapid redox reaction on the surface, rather than a slow Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation/deintercalation during sodium storage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407274-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407274-bib-0037_R_d91885445e1351" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Adv. Mater.">37</a>, <a href="#adma202407274-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407274-bib-0038_R_d91885445e1351" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Adv. Energy Mater.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To gain a better understanding of this high pseudocapacitive sodium storage mechanism of the NOCNTF-15 electrode, ex situ XPS testing was conducted at different discharge/charge stages. During the discharge to 0.01&nbsp;V, the intensity of the C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O peak in the O1s XPS spectra gradually decreased, and a new Na-KLL-Auger peak appeared at 535.5&nbsp;eV. In the case of the charging to 3&nbsp;V, the intensity of the C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O peak gradually increased, partially returning to the original stage (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202407274-fig-0006">6a–c</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29a,b</a>, Supporting Information), indicating the formation of SEI film and the reversible reaction between C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O and Na<sup>+</sup>, which can be described as C = O + Na<sup>+</sup> + e<sup>−</sup> ⇋ C-O-Na. Clear evidence was also provided by the changes in the XPS spectrum of Na 1s (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407274-fig-0006">6d–f</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29c,d</a>, Supporting Information), indicating that the peak intensity of C-O-Na gradually decreased with the charging level. These results showed that with the large specific surface area of NOCNTF-15, the C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O groups on the surface of CNTs exerted a beneficial role during the charge/discharge, thereby enhancing the Na<sup>+</sup> storage performance of the material.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407274-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407274-bib-0049_R_d91885445e1381" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Small">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To further elucidate the important role of C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O located on the surface of CNTs in enhancing the surface pseudocapacitive during the charge/discharge process and improving the adsorption storage performance of Na<sup>+</sup>, the adsorption energy (<i>E<sub>ad</sub></i>) of Na<sup>+</sup> at different active sites located on CNT and graphene (G) substrates was studied by DFT calculations. Computational models were constructed for CNTs and pyridine N (CNT/N6), pyrrolic N (CNT/N5), C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O (CNT/C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O) and C-OH (CNT/C-OH) located on the CNT substrate. In addition, computational models of G and pyridine N (G/N6), pyrrolic N (G/N5), C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O (G/C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O) and C-OH (G/C-OH) located on G substrate were constructed for comparison to reveal the enhancement of adsorption performance of high conductivity CNT substrate for Na<sup>+</sup> at different active sites (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a>, Supporting Information). The <i>-E<sub>ad</sub></i> of Na atom at CNT/N6, CNT/N5, CNT/C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O, and CNT/C-OH were calculated to be 1.81, 1.26, 2.37, and 1.44&nbsp;eV, respectively, values which were much larger than that of CNT (0.82&nbsp;eV) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407274-fig-0006">6g</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information), suggesting that surface modification of CNT with heteroatoms effectively improved their adsorption of Na atoms and enhanced their sodium storage performance. The <i>-E<sub>ad</sub></i> of different groups on the surface of CNT for Na atoms were in the order of C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O &gt; N6 &gt; C-OH &gt; N5, which is attributed to the fact that the lone pairs of electrons around the O atom of C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O can better serve as Lewis bases to adsorb Na atoms (Lewis acidic) through electron-donor-acceptor interactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407274-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407274-bib-0040_R_d91885445e1415" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Adv. Energy Mater.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, five Na atoms were stepwise placed into the above structural models to analyze and compare the multiple adsorption capacity of different groups on CNT and G substrates for Na atoms, respectively (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S32</a>, Supporting Information). The CNT substrate with higher conductivity was found to have stronger multiple adsorption capacity for sodium atoms than the G substrate, and as the number of sodium atoms in different adsorption active sites gradually increased, the C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O maintained the highest <i>-E<sub>ad</sub></i> for sodium atoms, thereby allowing the storage of more Na<sup>+</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407274-fig-0006">6g,h</a>). Therefore, DFT calculations further confirmed that materials with high electrical conductivity have higher adsorption energy for Na<sup>+</sup>.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202407274-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/98da046e-aa6d-4334-a1c8-ea414b69db64/adma202407274-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/98da046e-aa6d-4334-a1c8-ea414b69db64/adma202407274-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/bafd1100-d7f6-4046-ad51-293a499a16f7/adma202407274-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/98da046e-aa6d-4334-a1c8-ea414b69db64/adma202407274-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202407274-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202407274" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a–c) The ex situ XPS spectra of O 1s and d-f) Na 1s of the NOCNTF-15 electrode at the stage of pristine, discharge to 1.0&nbsp;V and discharge to 0.01&nbsp;V. Adsorption energy from one Na atom to five Na atoms over different models. g) CNT, CNT/N6, CNT/N5, CNT/C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O, CNT/C-OH and h) G, G/N6, G/N5, G/C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O, G/C-OH.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202407274-sec-0060">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202407274-sec-0060-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>We have reported a simple, low-energy (600&nbsp;°C) and high-yield (82&nbsp;wt.%) pyrolysis strategy affording a stable N-doped CNT non-hollow framework encapsulating Co nanoparticles (Co@NCNTF-15, 15 denotes the thickness of the liquid gallium layer during the pyrolysis is 15&nbsp;mm) from ZIF-67 based on the key use of liquid gallium as a protection layer against air, favoring heat transfer, and enabling retention of the carbon and nitrogen atoms in the framework. Upon acid treatment, the pyrolysis products underwent extensive C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O modification to form the N/O-enriched and open CNT non-hollow framework (NOCNTF-15), which exhibited excellent sodium storage performance as the anode of SIBs. The specific capacity could be stabilized at 185&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 21&nbsp;700 cycles at 10&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. It also maintained ultralong cycle stability and high-capacity retention even at 50&nbsp;°C. The NVPOF||NOCNTF-15 full cell displayed a high average working voltage of 4&nbsp;V and a high energy density of 233&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>. DFT calculations showed that the high electrical conductivity of CNT and the lone pair of electrons in the C&nbsp;=&nbsp;O group helped to enhance the adsorption energy of the material for Na<sup>+</sup>, which could adsorb more Na<sup>+</sup>. Our liquid gallium-assisted pyrolysis strategy is anticipated to have wider applicability and should advance the development of low-cost and high-yield CNTs and other carbon materials for high performance SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202407274-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202407274-sec-0070-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0080">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0090">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0100-title"> Synthesis of ZIF-67</h4>
                  
                  <p>Co(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O (11.64&nbsp;g) was dissolved in 1&nbsp;L of anhydrous methanol solution to give solution A. Then, 2-methylimidazole (13.13&nbsp;g) was dissolved in 1&nbsp;L of anhydrous methanol to give solution B. Solution A was rapidly added to solution B and stirred at room temperature for 24&nbsp;h. The precipitated product was collected by centrifugation at 8000&nbsp;rpm&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> and washed several times with anhydrous methanol. Finally, the product was dried in a vacuum oven at 60&nbsp;°C to obtain a purple powder (≈2.41&nbsp;g).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0110">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0110-title"> Synthesis of Co@NCNTF-x (x&nbsp;=&nbsp;5, 15 and 25)</h4>
                  
                  <p>ZIF-67 (≈0.042&nbsp;g) was placed in the bottom of a glass vial with a diameter of 5&nbsp;mm and then covered with liquid gallium at a height of 5&nbsp;mm above the ZIF-67. The glass vial was placed in a vacuum drying oven and evacuated at 60&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h to remove the voids and oxygen between the ZIF-67 layer and the liquid gallium layer. Then, different heights (0, 10, and 20&nbsp;mm) of liquid gallium were added to the glass vials. Subsequently, they were again evacuated in a vacuum oven at 60&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h to remove any air that may be present in the liquid gallium. Finally, the glass vials containing different heights of liquid gallium (5, 15, and 25&nbsp;mm) were placed in a muffle furnace and heated to 600&nbsp;°C at a heating rate of 2&nbsp;°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> for 4&nbsp;h. After cooling to room temperature, the upper layer of liquid gallium was recovered, and the black powder at the bottom of the glass vials was taken out and named Co@NCNTF-5, Co@NCNTF-15, and Co@NCNTF-25, and their yields were 77.1&nbsp;wt.%, 81.9&nbsp;wt.%, and 82.0&nbsp;wt.%, respectively.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0120-title"> Synthesis of NOCNTF-x (x&nbsp;=&nbsp;5, 15 and 25)</h4>
                  
                  <p>Co@NCNTF-5 (0.05&nbsp;g), Co@NCNT-15 (0.05&nbsp;g), or Co@NCNTF-25 (0.05&nbsp;g) was placed in a nitric acid solution of 9&nbsp;M, sonicated for 30&nbsp;min, and then stirred at 70&nbsp;°C for 4 days. The precipitates were then collected by centrifugation at 10000&nbsp;rpm&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> and washed several times by centrifugation with de-ionized water and anhydrous ethanol. Finally, the black powder was dried in a vacuum oven at 80&nbsp;°C to afford NOCNTF-5 (50.8&nbsp;wt.% yield), NOCNTF-15 (51.6&nbsp;wt.% yield) and NOCNTF-25 (51.4&nbsp;wt.% yield), respectively.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0130-title"> Synthesis of Co@NPCF</h4>
                  
                  <p>ZIF-67 (≈0.042&nbsp;g) was placed in an Ar atmosphere, heated to 600&nbsp;°C at a heating rate of 2&nbsp;°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> and held for 4&nbsp;h. After cooling to room temperature, the black powder was dried in a vacuum oven at 80&nbsp;°C to obtain Co@NPCF (45.5&nbsp;wt.% yield).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0140">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0140-title"> Synthesis of NOPCF</h4>
                  
                  <p>Co@NPCF (0.05&nbsp;g) was placed in a nitric acid solution at a concentration of 2&nbsp;M, sonicated for 30&nbsp;min, and then stirred at 45&nbsp;°C for 4 days. The precipitate was then collected by centrifugation at 10000&nbsp;rpm&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> and washed several times by centrifugation with deionized water and anhydrous ethanol. Finally, the black powder was dried in a vacuum oven at 80&nbsp;°C to obtain NOPCF (15.2&nbsp;wt.% yield).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0150">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0150-title"> Synthesis of ETCNT</h4>
                  
                  <p>ZIF-67 (≈0.042&nbsp;g) was dispersed in 10&nbsp;mL of anhydrous ethanol and the mixture was heated to 600&nbsp;°C in an Ar atmosphere at a heating rate of 2&nbsp;°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> and pyrolyzed for 4&nbsp;h. After cooling to room temperature, a black powder product is obtained and named ETCNT.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0160">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0160-title"> Synthesis of ZIF-8</h4>
                  
                  <p>Zn(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O (5.95&nbsp;g) was dissolved in 150&nbsp;mL of anhydrous methanol solution to give solution A. Then, 2-methylimidazole (6.16&nbsp;g) was dissolved in 150&nbsp;mL of anhydrous methanol to give solution B. Solution A was rapidly added to solution B and the mixture was stirred at room temperature for 24&nbsp;h. The precipitated product was collected by centrifugation at 8000&nbsp;rpm&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> and washed several times with anhydrous methanol. Finally, the product was dried in a vacuum oven at 60&nbsp;°C to obtain a white powder.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0170">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0170-title"> Synthesis of ZIF-8@ZIF-67</h4>
                  
                  <p>The as-prepared ZIF-8 (0.5&nbsp;g) were well-dispersed in 100&nbsp;mL of methanol. Then, methanolic solutions of Co(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub>·6H<sub>2</sub>O (5.82&nbsp;g, 50&nbsp;mL) and 2-methylimidazole (6.16&nbsp;g, 50&nbsp;mL) were injected stepwise into the above mixture, and the mixture was stirred at room temperature for 24&nbsp;h. ZIF-8@ZIF-67 dodecahedra were collected, washed with methanol three times and dried at 60&nbsp;°C in a vacuum oven.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0180">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0180-title"> Synthesis of ZIF-8@ZIF-67-Derived CNT Non-Hollow Frameworks</h4>
                  
                  <p>ZIF-8@ZIF-67 powder was placed in the bottom of a glass vial with a diameter of 5&nbsp;mm and then covered with liquid gallium at a height of 5&nbsp;mm above the ZIF-8@ZIF-67. The glass vial was placed in a vacuum drying oven and evacuated at 60&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h for the purpose of removing the voids and oxygen between the ZIF-8@ZIF-67 layer and the liquid gallium layer. Then, 10&nbsp;mm height of liquid gallium was added to the glass vials. Subsequently, they were again evacuated in a vacuum oven at 60&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h to remove any air that may be present in the liquid gallium. Finally, the glass vials containing 15&nbsp;mm thickness of liquid gallium was placed in a muffle furnace and heated to 600&nbsp;°C at a heating rate of 2&nbsp;°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> for 4&nbsp;h. After cooling to room temperature, the upper layer of liquid gallium was recovered, and the black powder at the bottom of the glass vials was taken out.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0190">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0190-title"> Synthesis of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>F</h4>
                  
                  <p>Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>F was synthesized according to previously reported method.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407274-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407274-bib-0050_R_d91885445e1632" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Adv. Mater.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> First, V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>C<sub>2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> (molar ratio&nbsp;=&nbsp;1:3) were dissolved in deionized water and stirred at 70&nbsp;°C for 1&nbsp;h. Then, stoichiometric amounts of NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub> and NaF were added to the solution and the pH value of the solution was subsequently adjusted to seven with ammonia. The resulting solution was transferred to a Teflon-lined stainless-steel autoclave and maintained at 170&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h. Finally, a light blue powder of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>2</sub>O<sub>2</sub>F was washed by distilled water, collected by centrifugation and dried in vacuo at 80&nbsp;°C.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202407274-sec-0200">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adma202407274-sec-0200-title"> Liquid Gallium Recovery Process</h4>
                  
                  <p>First, the liquid gallium was removed from the glass bottle using a plastic dropper, which left some liquid gallium on the wall of the glass bottle as gallium highly wetted silicate glass.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407274-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407274-bib-0022_R_d91885445e1674" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Sci. Adv.">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Then, some hot water (&gt;&nbsp;50&nbsp;°C) was added to the glass vial and placed it in an ultrasonic machine, where the liquid gallium attached to the glass wall was stripped off by ultrasonic vibration. The liquid gallium dispersed in the hot water was subsequently collected by centrifugation. The collected liquid gallium was dried in a vacuum oven at 100&nbsp;°C to remove the residual deionized water.</p>
                  
                  <p>Electrochemical measurements were carried out on all samples using the Land CT 2001 A instrument. DFT calculations were carried out using the Vienna ab initio Simulation Package (VASP). Details of the electrochemical tests, structural characterizations, and theoretical calculations are provided in Supporting Information.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
